Task instruction sent to agent 
# Revert Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) Fusions

**Repository:** pytorch
**Difficulty:** HARD
**Category:** cross_module_bug_fix



## Description

The Inductor compiler has pattern matching that fuses activation functions (ReLU, GELU) with Addmm (matrix multiply + bias add) operations into a single `_addmm_activation` call that leverages cuBLASLt's fused epilogue support. This optimization was intended to reduce kernel launches and memory traffic for common `Linear -> Activation` patterns.

However, the fusion causes regressions in certain model configurations and needs to be reverted. The revert must undo:
- The `_addmm_activation` pattern replacement in Inductor's lowering/decomposition passes
- The associated pattern matcher registrations for ReLU(Addmm) and GELU(Addmm)
- Any cuBLASLt epilogue fusion paths added for these patterns

Changes:
- 4 files modified
- 93 additions, 87 deletions

## Task

Revert the Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusion optimization. The `Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation` pattern replacement in the Inductor lowering pass for cuBLASLt fused epilogue support causes regressions and needs to be removed.

Changes:
- 4 files modified
- 93 additions, 87 deletions

Tasks:
1. Find the `_addmm_activation` pattern matching code in the Inductor lowering/decomposition passes
2. Remove the pattern matcher registrations for ReLU(Addmm) and GELU(Addmm) fusions
3. Remove any cuBLASLt epilogue fusion paths for these patterns
4. Verify your changes compile and match the expected fix

## Success Criteria

Code changes match the expected ground-truth fix.
Code follows repository conventions.
No regressions in existing functionality.
All 4 modified files updated correctly.

1479-
1480-    # The output of aten.addmm is contiguous, we need to match this behavior in the decomposition.
1481-    # The original implementation 'beta * self + out' would return a strided tensor if `self` is strided.
1482-    # We thus use `out`, the output of torch.mm, which is always contiguous, as the first argument for addition.
1483-    # This is relying on TensorIterator's behavior that it takes higher precedence on the stride of first input.
1484-    # Alternative, we can write `(beta * self + out).contiguous()`, but it introduces another copy in some cases.
1485-    # This implementation is not ideal, and we should revisit this when we have a better solution.
1486-    return out + beta * self

  1489→@register_decomposition(aten._addmm_activation)
  1490→@out_wrapper()
  1491→@pw_cast_for_opmath
  1492→def _addmm_activation(
  1493→    self: Tensor,
  1494→    mat1: Tensor,
  1495→    mat2: Tensor,
  1496→    beta: int = 1,
  1497→    alpha: int = 1,
  1498→    use_gelu: bool = False,
  1499→):
  1500→    out = addmm(self, mat1, mat2, beta, alpha)
  1501→    if use_gelu:
  1502→        if self.is_cuda:
  1503→            return aten.gelu(out, approximate="tanh")
  1504→        else:
  1505→            return aten.gelu(out)
  1506→    return aten.relu(out)
  1507→
  1508→
  1509→@register_decomposition(aten.addmv)
  1510→@out_wrapper(exact_dtype=True)
  1511→@pw_cast_for_opmath
  1512→def addmv(self: Tensor, mat1: Tensor, vec: Tensor, beta: int = 1, alpha: int = 1):
  1513→    if not self.is_floating_point() and not self.is_complex():
  1514→        beta = int(beta)
  1515→        alpha = int(alpha)
  1516→    out = alpha * torch.mv(mat1, vec)
  1517→    if beta == 0:
  1518→        return out

103-assistanttext-
Excellent! I've successfully reverted the Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusion optimization. Here's a summary of the changes:

## Changes Made

### 1. **torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py** (62 lines removed)
   - Removed the `register_addmm_activation_fusions()` function that registered pattern matchers for fusing `relu(addmm(...))` and `gelu(addmm(...), approximate="tanh")` into `_addmm_activation` calls
   - Removed the call to this function from `lazy_init()`

### 2. **torch/_decomp/decompositions.py** (20 lines removed)
   - Removed the `@register_decomposition(aten._addmm_activation)` function that decomposed fused `_addmm_activation` calls back into separate `addmm` + activation operations

### 3. **torch/_inductor/lowering.py** (1 line removed)
   - Removed the fallback lowering path for `aten._addmm_activation`

### 4. **test/inductor/test_pattern_matcher.py** (updated)
   - Updated `test_addmm_activation_fusion` test to reflect the reverted behavior:
     - Changed assertion from `assertIn("_addmm_activation", ...)` to `assertNotIn(...)`
     - Removed the max_autotune_gemm check since fusion no longer occurs
     - Updated comments to reflect that the fusion is disabled

### 5. **Auto-generated Pattern Files** (deleted)
   - `torch/_inductor/fx_passes/serialized_patterns/addmm_gelu_pattern.py` (43 lines)
   - `torch/_inductor/fx_passes/serialized_patterns/addmm_relu_pattern.py` (35 lines)

## Summary
- **6 files changed**: 4 modified, 2 deleted
- **Total changes**: 176 deletions, 4 insertions

The revert completely disables the Activation(Addmm) fusion optimization, reverting the compiler to use separate relu/gelu and addmm operations instead of the fused `_addmm_activation` kernel, which eliminates the regressions mentioned in the task.

Alternatively, we could just move the other device_put\n                # earlier in the graph, but that is not supported in fx graph yet.\n                noop_device_puts = [\n                    user\n                    for user in gpu_node.users\n                    if user.target is torch.ops.prims.device_put.default\n                    and user.args[1] == target_device\n                ]\n                for noop in noop_device_puts:\n                    noop.replace_all_uses_with(gpu_node)\n                    graph.erase_node(noop)\n\n        movable_constructors -= movable_cpu_placeholders\n        for node in movable_constructors:\n            kwargs = node.kwargs.copy()\n            kwargs[\"device\"] = target_device\n            node.kwargs = kwargs\n\n    def find_movable_constructors(\n        self, graph: fx.Graph, constructors: list[fx.Node]\n    ) -> OrderedSet[fx.Node]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Starting from the cpu constructors, iterate through the graph and test that all of their\n        downstream uses can safely be moved to cpu.\n        \"\"\"\n        cpu_indeg: dict[fx.Node, int] = self.get_cpu_indeg_count(graph)\n\n        # which constructors cannot be moved to gpu\n        cannot_move_to_gpu = OrderedSet[fx.Node]()\n\n        # For any node in the graph, which constructors does it have a dependency on\n        constructor_dependencies: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = defaultdict(\n            OrderedSet\n        )\n\n        # if a cpu node has a dependency on two different cpu constructors,\n        # then if either constructor cannot be moved to gpu, the other cannot as well.\n        # In this case any node with a dependency on one will have a dependency on the other\n        equal_constructor_sets: dict[fx.Node, OrderedSet[fx.Node]] = {\n            c: OrderedSet([c]) for c in constructors\n        }\n\n        def make_dependencies_equivalent(\n            set1: OrderedSet[fx.Node], set2: OrderedSet[fx.Node]\n        ) -> OrderedSet[fx.Node]:\n            # could use union find but not worth complexity here\n            set1.update(set2)\n            for obj in set1:\n                equal_constructor_sets[obj] = set1\n            return set1\n\n        queue: list[fx.Node] = list(constructors)\n\n        for c in queue:\n            constructor_dependencies[c].add(c)\n\n        while queue:\n            node = queue.pop()\n            dependencies = constructor_dependencies[node]\n\n            for user in node.users:\n                if self.cannot_be_moved(user):\n                    cannot_move_to_gpu.update(dependencies)\n                    break\n\n                # this node was used on a op which takes in multiple devices and output a gpu\n                # tensor. we can convert its cpu input to gpu without making further changes\n                if self.allow_cpu_device(user) and self.is_on_target_device(user):\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                elif (\n                    self.allow_inputs\n                    and self.all_inputs_are_cpu_scalar_or_on_target_device(user)\n                ):\n                    # this node takes only cpu scalar tensors or gpu tensors as inputs\n                    # and outputs a gpu tensor. we can convert its cpu scalar inputs to gpu\n                    # without making further changes\n                    del cpu_indeg[user]\n                else:\n                    # otherwise, we should continue look at its downstream uses\n                    cpu_indeg[user] -= 1\n                    if cpu_indeg[user] == 0:\n                        del cpu_indeg[user]\n                        queue.append(user)\n\n                unioned_set = make_dependencies_equivalent(\n                    dependencies, constructor_dependencies[user]\n                )\n                constructor_dependencies[user] = unioned_set\n\n        for node in cpu_indeg:\n            if constructor_dependencies[node]:\n                cannot_move_to_gpu.update(constructor_dependencies[node])\n\n        all_cannot_move_to_gpu = cannot_move_to_gpu.copy()\n        for constructor in cannot_move_to_gpu:\n            all_cannot_move_to_gpu.update(equal_constructor_sets[constructor])\n\n        return OrderedSet(constructors) - all_cannot_move_to_gpu\n\n\ndef move_constructors_to_gpu(graph: fx.Graph) -> None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Moves intermediary tensors which are constructed on the cpu to gpu when safe\n    \"\"\"\n\n    # cudagraph does not support cpu tensors. In this pass, we update the graph\n    # by explicitly moving cpu scalar tensors to gpu when profitable, relying on\n    # graph partition to split off this data copy, and cudagraphifying\n    # the remaining gpu ops.\n    allow_inputs_outputs = bool(\n        torch._inductor.config.triton.cudagraphs\n        and torch._inductor.config.graph_partition\n    )\n    ConstructorMoverPass(\n        get_gpu_type(),\n        allow_inputs=allow_inputs_outputs,\n        allow_outputs=allow_inputs_outputs,\n    )(graph)\n",

\"target should be a string representing the device type. \"\n            f\"Got: {type(target).__name__}\"\n        )\n\n    def allow_cpu_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n torch.ops.aten.slice_scatter.default,\n        )\n\n    def is_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        node_device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        return node_device is not None and node_device.type == self.target\n\n    def is_cpu_scalar_tensor(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n     # code gen with uint8 data type directly.\n        for input in inputs:\n            input.realize()\n        if all(len(input.get_size()) == 4 for input in inputs):\n            inputs, _ = x.data.unwrap_view()\n            else:\n                return x.data\n\n        if isinstance(x, ir.StorageBox):\n            return x.data\n\n        return x\n\n    def is_reduction(t):\n can_fuse_reduction(V.graph.get_buffer(read))\n                for read in t.get_read_names()\n            )\n        )\n\n    # fusing reducutions into computed concat buffer can cause regressions.\n    fusable_reduction = any(can_fuse_reduction(t) for t in inputs)\n\n    def should_lower_cat_input(x) -> bool:\n        # Unrealized inputs will not be storage and layouts, and we dont want to realize\n        # them in case we want to fuse\n        if ir.is_storage_and_layout(x):\n            storage, _ = ir.as_storage_and_layout(x, freeze=False)\n            return not ir.ConcatKernel.can_realize_into_without_copy(storage)\n\n        if isinstance(x, (TensorBox, ir.StorageBox)):\n            return should_lower_cat_input(unwrap_tensor(x))\n\n        if isinstance(x, ir.Pointwise):\n            return True\n\n        return False\n\n    if config.force_pointwise_cat:\n        return pointwise_cat(inputs, dim)\n\n    # TODO: We observed negative performance impact of pointwise_cat optimization on CPU so disabled it.\n    #             We will revisit this later after enabling vectorization on index_expr.\n    if cpu_device:\n        return TensorBox(ir.ConcatKernel.create(inputs, dim))\n\n    def op_count(x):\n        if isinstance(x, (TensorBox, ir.StorageBox)):\n            return op_count(unwrap_tensor(x))\n\n        # this will correspond to a direct memory read\n        if not isinstance(x, ir.Pointwise):\n            return 0\n\n        count = x.inner_fn_opcount().num_ops\n        for read in x.get_read_names():\n            count += op_count(V.graph.get_buffer(read))\n\n        return count\n\n    # as of inputs increase, possibility for register spilling also increases\n    # past a certain threshold of inputs we only fuse if the if the input kernels\n    # are simple\n    # not sure if we want to expose to users via config since logic may change in future\n    MAX_COMPLEX_POINTWISE_CAT = 8\n    MAX_SIMPLE_OP_COUNT = 2\n\n    def additional_pointwise_ops(op: torch._ops.OpOverload):\n        return op in (aten.cat.default, aten.constant_pad_nd.default)\n\n    if len(inputs) <=          is_pointwise_use(use, additional_pointwise_ops)\n            for use in V.current_node.users\n        )\n        # fuse in case we will be used in a pointwise node, and there are any inputs 1):\n    original_shape = input.get_size()\n    num_dims = len(original_shape)\n    dim1 = canonicalize_dim(idx=dim1, rank=num_dims)\n    dim2 = canonicalize_dim(idx=dim2, rank=num_dims)\n\n    check(\n        dim1 != dim2, lambda: f\"diagonal dimensions cannot be identical {dim1}, {dim2}\"\n    )\n\n    offset_negative = V.graph.sizevars.evaluate_expr(sympy.Lt(offset, 0))\n    if           0,  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n        )\n    else:\n        diag_size = V.graph.sizevars.evaluate_max(\n            V.graph.sizevars.evaluate_min(\n                original_shape[dim1],  base_idx = (0, offset)\n\n    sizes = [s for i, s in enumerate(original_shape) if i not in (dim1, dim2)]\n    sizes.append(diag_size)\n\n    def reindexer(idx):\n        diag_idx = idx[-1]\n        original_idx = [0] * len(original_shape)\n        cur_dim = 0\n        for d in range(num_dims):\n            if d == dim1:\n                original_idx[d] = diag_idx + base_idx[0]\n            elif mutate_to(target, src)\n    return output\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten.select, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef select(x, dim, idx):\n    idx = sympy.expand(idx)\n    size = sympy.expand(x.get_size()[dim])\n    actual_index = None\n\n    if V.graph.sizevars.guard_or_false(sympy.Lt(idx, 0)):\n        actual_index = idx + size\n    elif V.graph.sizevars.guard_or_false(sympy.Ge(idx, 0)):\n        actual_index = idx\n\n    if actual_index is not None:\n        if has_free_unbacked_symbols(idx):\n            # Inductor could generate accidental unbacked unsqueeze semantics. To resolve this,\n            # we use as_strided instead.\n            # Removing this branch will cause test_unbacked_select_index_with_check to fail.\n\n            # before accessing size, stride, and offset we need to realize.\n            x.realize()\n            new_size = x.get_size()\n            new_stride = x.get_stride()\n            new_storage_offset = x.get_layout().offset + new_stride[dim] * actual_index\n\n            del new_size[dim]\n            del new_stride[dim]\n            return as_strided(x, new_size, new_stride, new_storage_offset)\n        else:\n            # no need to clamp, this function handles negative indexing itself\n            slice_result = slice_(x, dim, actual_index, actual_index + 1, clamp=False)\n            return squeeze(slice_result, dim)\n\n    # before accessing size, stride, and offset we need to realize.\n    x.realize()\n    new_size = x.get_size()\n    new_stride = x.get_stride()\n    new_storage_offset = unbacked_offset_sym\n    buffer = ir.DynamicSelectStorageOffset(\n        unbacked_offset_sym,\n        idx,\n        x.get_layout().offset,\n        new_stride[dim],\n        x.get_size()[dim],\n        clamp=False,\n    )\n    buffer.name = V.graph.register_buffer(buffer)\n    V.graph.register_operation(buffer)\n\n    del new_size[dim]\n    del new_stride[dim]\n    return as_strided(x, new_size, new_stride, new_storage_offset)\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten.split, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef split(x, sizes, dim=0):\n    dim = _validate_dim(x, dim, 0)\n    sizes_ = sizes\n\n    # If sizes is an integer (or a SymInt), we turn it into a list of sizes\n    # by computing what the actual size of each chunk should be.\n    if not isinstance(sizes, (list, tuple)):\n        x_size = x.get_size()[dim]\n        chunks = V.graph.sizevars.guard_int(FloorDiv(x_size + sizes - 1, sizes))\n        sizes_ = [sizes] * chunks\n        # The last chunk might have a smaller size than the rest.\n        sizes_[-1] = x_size - (chunks - 1) * sizes\n\n    # From this point, we assume that the sum of the sizes of all chunks\n    # equals the size of the base tensor.\n    result = []\n    start = 0\n    for size in sizes_:\n        end = start + size\n        # type: ignore[arg-type]\n\n    new_dim_size = FloorDiv(dim_size - size, step) + 1\n    if sizevars.size_hint_or_throw(dim_size) > 0:\n        x.mark_reuse(\n            sizevars.size_hint_or_throw(CeilDiv(new_dim_size * size, dim_size))\n        )\n\n    out_size = [*sizes[:dim], new_dim_size, *sizes[dim + 1 :], size]\n\n    def reindexer(idx):\n        dim_idx = idx[-1] + idx[dim] * step\n        return (*idx[:dim], dim_idx, *idx[dim + 1 : -1])\n\n    return TensorBox(ir.GenericView.create(x, out_size, reindexer))\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten.unsqueeze, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef unsqueeze(x, dim):\n    dim = _validate_dim(x, dim, 1)\n    new_shape = list(x.get_size())\n    new_shape.insert(dim, sympy.S.One)\n    return view(x, new_shape)\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten.unsqueeze_, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef unsqueeze_(x, dim):\n    val = unsqueeze(x, dim)\n    assert isinstance(x, TensorBox)\n    assert isinstance(val, TensorBox)\n    x.data = val.data\n    return x\n\n\ndef _validate_dim(x, dim, offset=0):\n    dim = V.graph.sizevars.shape_env.evaluate_expr(sympy.sympify(dim))\n    ndim = len(x.get_size())\n    if dim < 0:\n        dim += ndim + offset\n    assert 0 <= dim < ndim + offset\n    return dim\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten.glu)\ndef glu(x, dim=-1):\n    dim = _validate_dim(x, dim, 0)\n    # Performance may be worse than eager.\"\n    )\n\n\n# There are some types (CPU) which we accept as input but not as\n# output.\ndef unsupported_input_tensor(t: torch.Tensor, node=None):\n    \"Do not support reading or writing to this tensor\"\n    if t.is_complex():\n        # Complex views are supported with IR ComplexView\n        _warn_complex_not_supported()\n        return True\n\n    if t.is_meta:\n        return True\n\n    if t.is_sparse:\n        return True\n\n    if t.dtype == torch.float8_e8m0fnu:\n        if not node:\n            return True\n\n        # Custom fallback lowering\n    if node.target is aten.view_as_complex.default:\n        return False\n\n    if node.op == \"placeholder\":\n        return False\n\n    # We should be able to remove this special case once `disable_cpp_codegen` is killed.\n    if node.target is aten.lift_fresh_copy.default:\n        return False\n\n    def check_skip_condition(inp_out_node, is_output):\n        if not isinstance(inp_out_node, torch.fx.Node):\n            return False\n\n        if \"val\" not in inp_out_node.meta:\n            return False\n\n        for meta in pytree.tree_leaves(inp_out_node.meta[\"val\"]):\n            if not isinstance(meta, torch._subclasses.FakeTensor):\n                continue\n\n            if is_output:\n                if unsupported_output_tensor(meta, node):\n                    return True\n            else:\n                if unsupported_input_tensor(meta, node):\n                    return True\n\n        return False\n\n    # likely to be triggered preferentially on one CI config over another.\n        if torch._dynamo.config.suppress_errors:\n            torch._dynamo.config.suppress_errors = False\n            log.warning(\n                \"A make_fallback error occurred in suppress_errors config,\"\n                \" and suppress_errors is being disabled to surface it.\"\n            )\n        raise AssertionError(\n            f\"make_fallback({op}): a decomposition exists, we should switch to it.\"\n            \" To fix this error, either add a decomposition to core_aten_decompositions (preferred)\"\n            \" or inductor_decompositions, and delete the corresponding `make_fallback` line.\"\n            \" Get help from the inductor team if unsure, don't pick arbitrarily to unblock yourself.\",\n        )\n\n    def register_fallback(op_overload):\n        add_needs_realized_inputs(op_overload)\n        if layout_constraint is not None:\n            add_layout_constraint(op_overload, layout_constraint)\n        return register_lowering(op_overload, type_promotion_kind=None)(\n            fallback_handler(op_overload)\n        )\n\n    if isinstance(op, torch._ops.OpOverloadPacket):\n        for ol in op.overloads():\n            op_overload = getattr(op, ol)\n            register_fallback(op_overload)\n    elif isinstance(op, (torch._ops.OpOverload, torch._ops.HigherOrderOperator)):\n        register_fallback(op)\n    else:\n        raise RuntimeError(f\"Unsupported fallback {op} with type {type(op)}\")\n\n\ndef philox_rand_offset(shape):\n    \"\"\"\n    TorchInductor offset calculation differs from PyTorch eager offset\n    calculation for random ops (tl.rand vs torch.rand). config.fallback_random\n    assert mode in (\"rand\", \"randn\")\n    size = [*size]\n    dtype = torch.float32\n    device = seed.get_device_or_error()\n    random_pos = ir.FixedLayout(\n        device, dtype, size, ir.FlexibleLayout.contiguous_strides(size), offset=offset\n    ).make_indexer()\n    seed_loader = seed.make_loader()\n\n    def inner_fn(index):\n        return getattr(ops, mode)(\n            seed_loader([]),\n            ops.index_expr(random_pos(index), torch.int32),\n        )\n\n    result = Pointwise.create(\n        device=device,\n        dtype=dtype,\n int, high: int, size: list[int], seed: TensorBox, *, offset: int = 0\n):\n    assert not config.fallback_random\n    size = [*size]\n    dtype = torch.int64\n    device = seed.get_device_or_error()\n    random_pos = ir.FixedLayout(\n        device, dtype, size, ir.FlexibleLayout.contiguous_strides(size), offset=offset\n    ).make_indexer()\n    seed_loader = seed.make_loader()\n\n    def _boundaries_helper(tb: TensorBox) -> tuple[str, sympy.Expr, sympy.Expr, sympy.Expr]:\n    # Calculate the maximum offset for the boundaries tensor\n    # For a strided tensor, this is sum((size[i] - 1) * stride[i]) + stride[-1]\n    # This ensures the mask check in bucketize_binary_search works correctly\n    # for both contiguous and non-contiguous tensors.\n    size = tb.get_size()\n    stride = tb.get_stride()\n    max_offset = sum((s - 1) * st for s, st in zip(size, stride)) + stride[-1]\n    return (\n        tb.get_name(),\n        size[-1],\n        max_offset,\n        stride[-1],\n    )\n\n\ndef _sorter_helper(tb: TensorBox) -> tuple[str, sympy.Expr]:\n    return tb.get_name(), tb.get_stride()[-1]\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten.searchsorted.Tensor, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef searchsorted(\n    sorted_sequence: TensorBox,\n    self: TensorBox,\n    *,\n    out_int32: bool = False,\n    right: bool = False,\n    side: Optional[str] = None,\n    sorter: Optional[TensorBox] = None,\n) -> Union[TensorBox, ShapeAsConstantBuffer]:\n    validate_bucketize = lambda tb: V.graph.has_feature(  # noqa: E731\n        tb, BackendFeature.BUCKETIZE\n    )\n    if (\n        not validate_bucketize(sorted_sequence)\n        or not validate_bucketize(self)\n        or (sorter is not None and not validate_bucketize(sorter))\n    ):\n        return fallback_handler(aten.searchsorted.Tensor, add_to_fallback_set=False)(\n            sorted_sequence,\n            self,\n            out_int32=out_int32,\n            right=right,\n            side=side,\n            sorter=sorter,\n        )\n\n    # If side is present, override the value of right if needed.  This assumes that\n    # validation of the two options being non-contradictory is already done by the\n    # searchsorted meta-function.\n    if side is not None and side == \"right\":\n        right = True\n\n    index_dtype = torch.int32 if out_int32 else torch.int64\n    values_loader = self.make_loader()\n\n    # The entire sorted_sequence tensor needs to be used by ops.bucketize, so we need to\n    # realize it into global memory; or in other words, we can't guarantee that\n    # sorted_sequence.get_name() (used below) will exist unless we call\n    # sorted_sequence.realize().\n    sorted_sequence.realize()\n\n    if sorter is not None:\n        sorter.realize()\n\n    if len(sorted_sequence.get_size()) == 1:\n\n        def inner_fn(idx):\n            val = values_loader(idx)\n            return ops.bucketize(\n                val,\n                _boundaries_helper(sorted_sequence),\n                0,\n                index_dtype,\n                right,\n                sorter=None if sorter is None else _sorter_helper(sorter),\n                sorter_indices=None if sorter is None else 0,\n            )\n\n    else:\n\n        def inner_fn(idx):\n            val = values_loader(idx)\n\n            # Get index to the beginning of the sorted sequence within a flattened\n            # version of the array.\n            def get_flattened_index(tb: TensorBox):\n                strides = tb.get_stride()\n                return ops.index_expr(\n                    functools.reduce(\n                        operator.add, (s * i for s, i in zip(strides[:-1], idx[:-1]))\n                    ),\n                    index_dtype,\n                )\n\n            return ops.bucketize(\n                val,\n                _boundaries_helper(sorted_sequence),\n                get_flattened_index(sorted_sequence),\n                index_dtype,\n                right,\n                sorter=None if sorter is None else _sorter_helper(sorter),\n                sorter_indices=None if sorter is None else get_flattened_index(sorter),\n            )\n\n    device = self.get_device()\n    result = Pointwise.create(\n        device=device,\n        dtype=index_dtype,\n        inner_fn=inner_fn,\n        ranges=self.shape,\n    )\n    # see [NOTE: inductor bucketize realize]\n    result.realize()\n\n    return result\n\n\n@register_lowering(\n    aten.bucketize, type_promotion_kind=ELEMENTWISE_TYPE_PROMOTION_KIND.NO_OPMATH\n)\ndef bucketize(\n    input: TensorBox,\n    boundaries: TensorBox,\n    *,\n    out_int32: bool = False,\n    right: bool = False,\n):\n    assert len(boundaries.get_size()) == 1\n\n    if not (\n        V.graph.has_feature(input, BackendFeature.BUCKETIZE)\n        and V.graph.has_feature(boundaries, BackendFeature.BUCKETIZE)\n    ):\n        return fallback_handler(aten.bucketize.Tensor, add_to_fallback_set=False)(\n            input, boundaries, out_int32=out_int32, right=right\n        )\n\n    # The entire boundaries tensor needs to be used by ops.bucketize, so we\n    # need to realize it into global memory; or in other words, we can't\n    # guarantee that boundaries.get_name() (used below) will exist unless\n    # we call boundaries.realize().\n    boundaries.realize()\n    device = input.get_device()\n    input_loader = input.make_loader()\n\n    index_dtype = torch.int32 if out_int32 else torch.int64\n\n    def inner_fn(index):\n        val = input_loader(index)\n        indices = ops.bucketize(\n            val,\n            _boundaries_helper(boundaries),\n            0,\n            index_dtype,\n            right,\n        )\n\n        return indices\n\n    result = Pointwise.create(\n        device=device,\n        dtype=index_dtype,\n        inner_fn=inner_fn,\n        ranges=input.get_size(),\n    )\n\n    # [NOTE: inductor bucketize realize]\n    # bucketize_binary_search is relatively expensive, so we don't want to re-compute\n    # it unnecessarily. If we run bucketize() and then broadcast the result, we don't\n    # want this to be fused into a large number of duplicate bucketize() computations\n    # for each of the elements in the result.\n    #\n    # If no broadcasting occurs, fusions can still occur in scheduler.py\n    result.realize()\n\n    return result\n\n\ndef require_dense(_, *args, **kwargs):\n    args, kwargs = ir.IRNode, ir.ExternKernel.require_channels_last, (args, kwargs)\n    )\n    return args, kwargs\n\n\ndef constrain_to_fake_tensor(arg, fake_arg):\n    if fake_arg is None:\n        return arg\n    if isinstance(fake_arg, FakeScriptObject):\n        return arg\n    if isinstance(arg, ir.IRNode):\n        meta_stride_expr = [\n            s.node.expr if isinstance(s, torch.SymInt) else s for s in fake_arg[key]) for key in arg}\n    elif isinstance(arg, (tuple, list)):\n        return type(arg)(\n            constrain_to_fake_tensor(a, f_a) for (a, f_a) in zip(arg, fake_arg)\n        )\n def apply_constraint(arg, fx_arg):\n        if isinstance(arg, ir.IRNode):\n            stride_order = ir.get_stride_order(\n                fx_arg.meta[\"val\"].stride(), V.graph.sizevars.shape_env\n            )\n            return ir.ExternKernel.require_stride_order(arg, stride_order)\n        if isinstance(arg, dict):\n            return {key: apply_constraint(arg[key], fx_arg[key]) for key in arg}\n        return arg\n\n    args = tuple(\n        apply_constraint(arg, fx_arg) for arg, fx_arg in zip(args, fx_node.args)\n    )\n    kwargs = {k: apply_constraint(v, fx_node.kwargs[k]) for k, v in kwargs.items()}\n    return args, kwargs\n\n\ndef sdpa_constraint(fx_node, *args, **kwargs):\n    # sdpa requires dense last dimension]\n\n    def apply_constraint(idx, arg, fx_arg):\n        if not isinstance(arg, ir.IRNode):\n            return arg\n\n        meta_val = fx_arg.meta[\"val\"]\n        meta_stride_expr = [\n            s.node.expr if isinstance(s, torch.SymInt) else s for s in meta_val.stride()\n        ]\n        shape_env = V.graph.sizevars.shape_env\n        stride_order = ir.get_stride_order(meta_val.stride(), shape_env)\n\n        if stride_order and stride_order[-1] != 0:\n            # contiguous stride order\n            stride_order = list(reversed(range(len(arg.get_size()))))\n\n        if (\n            fx_node.target\n            == aten._scaled_dot_product_efficient_attention_backward.default\n            and idx in (0, 5)\n        ):\n            assert len(stride_order) == 4\n            # The 0 and 5th arguments for aten._scaled_dot_product_efficient_attention_backward.default\n            # are for out and gradient_out. They have to be in\n            # (3, 1, 2, 0) stride order. Otherwise the kernel will crash.\n            # Check https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/138772\n            stride_order = (3, 1, 2, 0)\n\n        if not meta_val.is_cuda:\n            return ir.ExternKernel.require_stride_order(arg, stride_order)\n\n        # This is the minimum alignment required by SDPA kernels for attention_bias.\n        # This value can be found in pytorch/aten/src/ATen/native/transformers/attention.cpp preprocess_mask\n        ALIGNMENT = 8\n\n        # effn_attn_fwd does requires dense last dim, not just alignment\n        effn_attn_fwd_bias = (\n            fx_node.target\n            == torch.ops.aten._scaled_dot_product_efficient_attention.default\n            and idx == 3\n        )\n\n        assert isinstance(arg, TensorBox)\n        if len(arg.get_size()) not in (3, 4):\n            return arg\n\n        is_aligned_tensor = ir.is_aligned_realized_tensor(arg, ALIGNMENT)\n        if is_aligned_tensor:\n            return ir.try_match_insignificant_strides(\n                ir.ExternKernel.realize_input(arg), meta_stride_expr\n            )\n\n        if (\n            isinstance(arg, IRNode)\n            and arg.maybe_get_stride() is not None\n            and is_aligned_tensor\n        ):\n            return ir.try_match_insignificant_strides(\n                ir.ExternKernel.realize_input(arg), meta_stride_expr\n            )\n\n        if effn_attn_fwd_bias:\n            out_size = list(arg.get_size())\n\n            expanded_dims = []\n            # We require a dense last dimension, but the other strides\n            # can be expanded, which results in a smaller tensor\n            maybe_stride = arg.maybe_get_stride()\n            for i in range(len(arg.get_size()) - 1):\n                if V.graph.sizevars.statically_known_equals(meta_stride_expr[i], 0) or (\n                    maybe_stride is not None\n                    and V.graph.sizevars.statically_known_equals(maybe_stride[i], 0)\n                ):\n                    expanded_dims.append(i)\n\n            # Now, pad strides to alignment\n            out_strides = [-1] * len(out_size)\n            out_strides[-1] = 1\n            stride = 1\n            for i in range(len(out_size) - 2, -1, -1):\n                if out_strides[i + 1] != 0:\n                    stride = stride * out_size[i + 1]\n\n                # the expanded dims still need to be aligned, if they are,\n                # we can make them expanded by setting the stride equal to 0\n                if i in expanded_dims:\n                    if V.graph.sizevars.statically_known_equals(\n                        out_strides[i + 1] % ALIGNMENT, 0\n                    ):\n                        out_strides[i] = 0\n                        continue\n\n                if not V.graph.sizevars.statically_known_equals(stride % ALIGNMENT, 0):\n                    stride = ceildiv(stride, ALIGNMENT) * ALIGNMENT\n\n                out_strides[i] = stride\n\n            return ir.ExternKernel.require_exact_strides(arg, out_strides)\n\n        if is_aligned_tensor:\n            return ir.try_match_insignificant_strides(\n                ir.ExternKernel.realize_input(arg), meta_stride_expr\n            )\n\n        if (\n            isinstance(arg, IRNode)\n            and arg.maybe_get_stride() is not None\n            and is_aligned_tensor\n        ):\n            return ir.try_match_insignificant_strides(\n                ir.ExternKernel.realize_input(arg), meta_stride_expr\n            )\n\n        def is_aligned(x):\n            return V.graph.sizevars.guard_or_false(\n                sympy.Eq(Mod(x.get_size()[-1], ALIGNMENT), 0)\n            )\n\n        if isinstance(arg.data, ir.BaseView):\n            if not is_aligned(arg):\n                if is_aligned(arg.unwrap_view()):\n                    return ir.try_match_insignificant_strides(\n                        ir.ExternKernel.realize_input(arg), meta_stride_expr\n                    )\n\n        return ir.ExternKernel.require_stride_order(arg, stride_order)\n\n    args = tuple(\n        apply_constraint(idx, arg, fx_arg)\n        for idx, (arg, fx_arg) in enumerate(zip(args, fx_node.args))\n    )\n    kwargs = {k: apply_constraint(-1, v, fx_node.kwargs[k]) for k, v in kwargs.items()}\n    return args, kwargs\n\n\n# WIP\nmake_fallback(aten._adaptive_avg_pool3d)  # promote the first input's dtype.\n@register_lowering(aten.copy, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef copy(self, src, non_blocking=False):\n    if not isinstance(src, ir.IRNode):\n        src = tensor(src, dtype=self.get_dtype(), device=self.get_device())\n    x = src\n    if self.get_device() != src.get_device():\n        # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]\n        x = to_device(x, _local_scalar_dense(data):\n    # This is interesting!  Most lowerings return tensors, so you can just\n    # return the buffer you allocated and it will get used (or not used, if\n    # it's dead.)  But _local_scalar_dense (aka item) returns an int,\n    # not a Tensor, so you would have a type mismatch if you return a buffer;\n    # we are obligated to return a sympy expression instead.  However,\n    # we need to actually codegen the .item() call somehow.  We do this\n    # by registering a faux buffer for the DynamicScalar IR node, which is\n    # solely responsible for generating this .item().  The buffer is\n    # not used for anything (notice we discard it); at codegen time,\n    # the \"buffer\" just gets assigned None.\n    unbacked_bindings = resolve_unbacked_bindings(\n        V.graph.sizevars.shape_env, V.graph.current_node.meta[\"unbacked_bindings\"]\n    )\n    assert unbacked_bindings is not None\n    assert len(unbacked_bindings) == 1, unbacked_bindings\n    # NB: Have to be very careful here.  V.graph.current_node.meta[\"val\"]\n    # seemingly also contains a symbol which you want to do binding for,\n    # but it actually isn't.  In particular, if we have later performed\n    # a deferred runtime assert saying that u0 == s0, you will actually\n    # see s0 from expr!  This is bad because we need to actually generate\n    # the assert that says u0 == s0, so we need to know where to get u0\n    # from (this call).  In particular, we must use unbacked_bindings, which\n    # is guaranteed to have the original, unreplaced symbol in question.\n    #\n    # NB2: Another thing we have to be very careful about are symbol bindings\n    # that require nontrivial refinement, e.g., when you have a binding site\n    # x: Sym(u0 * 4) = y.item().  Here, the code generation must do a division\n    # in order to appropriately bind u0.  This is communicated via the keypath\n    # in unbacked_bindings, and we need to hold onto it in order to generate\n    # code appropriately for this case.\n    binding_sym, keypath = next(iter(unbacked_bindings.items()))\n    buffer = ir.DynamicScalar(binding_sym, keypath, data)\n    buffer.name = V.graph.register_buffer(buffer)\n    V.graph.register_operation(buffer)\n    # NB: the replaced expr is OK to use directly downstream, we want\n    # simplifications in this case!\n    val = V.graph.current_node.meta[\"val\"]\n    if isinstance(val, (torch.SymInt, torch.SymFloat, torch.SymBool)):\n        return val.node.expr\n    else:\n        return sympy.sympify(val)\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten._assert_scalar)\ndef _assert_scalar(data, msg):\n    # type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef embedding(weight, indices, padding_idx=-1, scale_grad_by_freq=False, sparse=False):\n    if sparse:\n        return fallback_handler(aten.embedding.default)(\n i.get_dtype() in (torch.int64, torch.int32, torch.bool, torch.uint8)\n        for i in indices\n        if i is not None\n    ), (\n        f\"indices must be int64, byte or bool. Got {[i.get_dtype() for i in indices if i is not None]}\"\n    )\n    if any(\n        i.get_dtype() in (torch.bool, torch.uint8) for i in indices if i is not None\n    ):\n        raise NotImplementedError(\"Fallback for bool indices\")\n\n    valid_idxs = [i for i, x in enumerate(indices) if isinstance(x, TensorBox)]\n    assert len(valid_idxs) > 0, \"requires at least 1 non-None index\"\n    new_indices = [None] * len(indices)\n    for i, x in zip(valid_idxs, broadcast_tensors(*[indices[i] for i in valid_idxs])):\n        # Eager allows indices to be CPU tensor when running on CUDA\n        # FIXME: Calling to_device(x, device) should work but\n        # test_advancedindex_mixed_cpu_devices still fails\n        if x.get_device() != device:\n            raise NotImplementedError(\"Fallback when indices is on a different device\")\n        new_indices[i] = x\n    return new_indices, valid_idxs\n\n\ndef index_output_size_and_inner_fn(\n    x_size,\n    indices,\n    tensor_indices,\n    tensor_size,\n    indices_loaders,\n    indexed_size,\n    x_loader,\n    check,\n    wrap_neg=True,\n):\n    # Note that behavior of indexing differs when there are non consecutive\n    # tensors. In this case, the tensor index is pulled to the beginning.\n    #\n    # Suppose a = torch.arange(3 * 4 * 5 * 6 * 7).view(3, 4, 5, 6, 7)\n    #         x = torch.tensor[1,2]\n    # Then, a[:,x,:,x,:] will have shape 2,3,5,7 as due to x,:,x then 2 will\n    # be pulled to the front.\n    non_consecutive_tensors = False\n    for previous, current in itertools.pairwise(tensor_indices):\n        if current - previous != 1:\n            non_consecutive_tensors = True\n\n    output_size = [x_size[i] for i, val in enumerate(indices) if val is None]\n    output_size = [*output_size, *x_size[len(output_size) + len(tensor_indices) :]]\n\n    first_tensor_index = tensor_indices[0]\n    if non_consecutive_tensors:\n        output_size = tensor_size + output_size\n    else:\n        output_size = (\n            output_size[:first_tensor_index]\n            + tensor_size\n            + output_size[first_tensor_index:]\n        )\n\n    def fn(idx):\n        assert len(idx) == len(output_size)\n        assert len(indices_loaders) == len(indexed_size)\n\n        rank = len(tensor_size)\n        new_index = []\n        first_tensor_index = tensor_indices[0]\n        start_offset = 0 if non_consecutive_tensors else first_tensor_index\n        next_idx = 0\n        for i in range(tensor_indices[-1] + 1):\n            if i == start_offset:\n                next_idx += rank\n            if indices[i] is None:\n                assert next_idx < len(idx)\n                new_index.append(idx[next_idx])\n                next_idx += 1\n            else:\n                loader = indices_loaders[i]\n                assert loader is not None\n                size = indexed_size[i]\n                new_index.append(\n                    ops.indirect_indexing(\n                        loader(idx[start_offset : start_offset + rank]),\n                        size,\n                        check=check,\n                        wrap_neg=wrap_neg,\n                    )\n                )\n        new_index = [\n            *new_index,\n            *idx[next_idx:],\n        ]\n        return new_index if x_loader is None else x_loader(new_index)\n\n    return output_size, fn\n\n\ndef index_impl(x, indices, check):\n    output_size, inner_fn, _ = index_impl_helper(x, indices, check)\n\n    return Pointwise.create(\n        device=x.get_device(),\n        dtype=x.get_dtype(),\n        inner_fn=inner_fn,\n        ranges=output_size,\n    )\n\n\ndef index_impl_helper(x, indices, check, wrap_neg=True):\n    assert isinstance(indices, (list, tuple))\n    x_loader = x.make_loader()\n    indices, tensor_indices = check_and_broadcast_indices(indices, x.get_device())\n    assert len(tensor_indices) > 0, \"Must have at least one valid idx\"\n\n    indices_loaders = [i.make_loader() if i is not None else None for i in indices]\n    # no guards on output size, all the guards are set in broadcast_tensors\n\n    # We can use the first one since they are all required to be the same size\n    tensor_size = list(indices[tensor_indices[0]].get_size())\n\n    x_size = x.get_size()\n\n    indexed_size = [x_size[i] for i in range(len(indices)) if indices[i] is not None]\n    if check and 0 in indexed_size and 0 not in tensor_size:\n        raise IndexError(\"index is out of bounds for dimension with size 0\")\n\n    indexed_size = [x_size[i] for i in range(len(indices))]\n    output_size, index_inner_fn = index_output_size_and_inner_fn(\n        x_size,\n        indices,\n        tensor_indices,\n        tensor_size,\n float\n) -> Optional[TensorBox]:\n    \"\"\"\n    This optimization changes the semantics of padding from 'clone'\n    style to 'view' style.\n\n    Thanks to functionalization, this change can still maintain numerical\n    correctness.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def _padding_can_be_fused():\n        \"\"\"\n        Conservatively check if padding can be fused with downstream op.\n        1. if the downstream op is a sum, then there is little benefit to\n           do inplace padding\n        2. if the downstream op is a matmul, doing inplace padding can\n           save membw.\n        \"\"\"\n        current_node = V.graph.current_node\n        if current_node is None:\n            return True  # be conservative\n        users = tuple(current_node.users)\n        if len(users) == 1 and users[0].target in (\n            aten.mm.default,\n            aten.addmm.default,\n        ):\n            return False\n\n        return True  # be conservative\n\n    if _padding_can_be_fused():\n        return None\n\n    # Only handle 2D case for now\n    if len(padding) != 4 or len(x.get_size()) != 2:\n        return None\n\n    # No harm to realize since we already know that\n    # the op can not be fused into the single user.\n    # It need to be realized later anyways.\n    x.realize()\n\n    # If x is a view (e.g. a SliceView), realizing it just realizing the\n    # underlying storage. x itself is still a view.\n    if (\n        not isinstance(x, ir.TensorBox)\n        or not isinstance(x.data, ir.StorageBox)\n        or not (\n            isinstance(x.data.data, ir.ComputedBuffer)\n            or (\n                config.can_inplace_pad_graph_input\n                and isinstance(x.data.data, ir.InputBuffer)\n            )\n        )\n        or not x.data.data.name\n    ):\n        return None\n    x.freeze_layout()\n\n    _, layout = ir.as_storage_and_layout(x)\n    strides = layout.stride\n    if strides[1] != 1:\n        return None\n\n    if padding[0] != 0 or padding[2] != 0 or padding[3] != 0:\n        return None\n\n    npad = padding[1]\n    if npad == 0:\n        return None\n\n    stride0 = strides[0]\n    rowsize = layout.size[1]\n\n    if stride0 < rowsize + npad:\n        return None\n\n    bufname = x.data.data.name\n    padded_size = [layout.size[0], layout.size[1] + npad]\n    V.graph.buffer_to_padded_size[bufname] = padded_size\n    resized_x = as_strided(\n        x,\n        padded_size,\n        layout.stride,\n        layout.offset,\n    )\n\n    sliced_x = slice_(resized_x, dim=1, start=rowsize, end=rowsize + npad, clamp=False)\n    fill_(sliced_x, fill_value)\n\n    counters[\"inductor\"][\"inplace_padding\"] += 1\n    return resized_x\n\n\n@register_lowering(aten.constant_pad_nd, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef constant_pad_nd(x, padding, fill_value=0):\n    assert (len(padding) % 2) == 0\n    if all(p == 0 for p in if can not inplace the padding\n\n    sizes = x.get_size()\n\n    bounds = list(reversed(list(zip(padding[::2], padding[1::2]))))\n    n = len(sizes) - len(bounds)\n\n    # if padding is a complicated     )\n        if V.graph.sizevars.size_hint((x_alt - 1) * stride[i] - x - padding[i]) >= 0:\n            # Sliding windows must start within the input or left padding\n            x_alt -= 1  # type: kernel_sz[dim]\n    samples_loader = samples.make_loader()\n\n    def load(prefix, i):\n        # Handle indexing for samples tensor correctly for different input dimensions\n        # samples tensor always has shape (N, C, 2) for fractional_max_pool2d where:\n        # - N=1 for 3D inputs (C,H,W), N=batch_size for 4D inputs (N,C,H,W)\n        # - C=num_channels\n        # - 2 for the two spatial dimensions (height, width)\n        samples_shape = samples.get_size()\n\n        if len(samples_shape) == 3:  # Expected: (N, C, 2)\n            if len(prefix) == 1:\n                # 3D input case: prefix=(channel,), samples=(1, C, 2)\n                # Access: samples[0, channel, dim]\n                sample = samples_loader([0, prefix[0], ndims - 1 - dim])\n            elif len(prefix) >= 2:\n                # 4D+ input case: prefix=(batch, channel, ...), samples=(batch, C, 2)\n                # Access: samples[batch, channel, dim]\n                sample = samples_loader([prefix[0], prefix[1], ndims - 1 - dim])\n            else:\n                # Edge case - shouldn't happen for valid fractional pooling\n                sample = samples_loader([0, 0, ndims - 1 - dim])\n        else:\n            # Fallback for unexpected tensor shapes\n            sample = samples_loader([*prefix, ndims - 1 - dim])\n        i_expr = ops.index_expr(i, samples.get_dtype())\n        diff = ops.index_expr(in_sz - kernel_sz, torch.int64)\n        out_sz_expr = ops.index_expr(out_sz - 1, torch.int64)\n        alpha = ops.truediv(\n            ops.to_dtype(diff, torch.float64), ops.to_dtype(out_sz_expr, torch.float64)\n        )\n        alpha = ops.where(ops.eq(out_sz_expr, 0), 0, alpha)\n        seq_i = ops.trunc((i_expr + sample) * alpha) - ops.trunc(sample * alpha)\n        seq_i = ops.to_dtype(seq_i, torch.int64)\n        mask = ops.lt(i_expr, out_sz_expr)\n        return ops.indirect_indexing(ops.where(mask, seq_i, diff), sympy.sympify(in_sz))\n\n    return        count_include_pad,\n            divisor_override,\n        )\n\n    def compute_pool_size_without_padding(ph, pw):\n        \"\"\"\n        This computes the scaling factor that we will divide )\n\n                    if divisor_override is not None:\n                        scale = divisor_override\n                    elif count_include_pad or not had_padding:\n                        scale = kernel_size[0] * kernel_size[1] * kernel_size[2]\n                    else:\n                        scale = compute_pool_size_without_padding(pd, ph, pw)\n\n                    part =                 ops.minimum(\n                                        pd, ops.sub(pdend, ops.constant(1, torch.int32))\n                                    ),\n                                    pooled_depth,\n                                    check=False,\n                                ),\n                                ops.indirect_indexing(\n                                    ops.minimum(\n                                        ph, ops.sub(phend, ops.constant(1, torch.int32))\n                                    ),\n                                    pooled_height,\n                                    check=False,\n                                ),\n                                ops.indirect_indexing(\n                                    ops.minimum(\n                                        pw, ops.sub(pwend, ops.constant(1, torch.int32))\n                                    ),\n                                    pooled_width,\n                 gradient = ops.where(\n                            mask, part, ops.constant(0.0, torch.float32)\n                        )\n                    else:\n                        gradient dtype=dtype,\n        inner_fn=fn,\n        ranges=new_size,\n    )\n    return rv\n\n\ndef _validate_reduction_axis(x, axis):\n    size = x.get_size()\n    if isinstance(axis, int):\n        axis = def loader(index, reduction_index):\n        assert len(reduction_index) == len(reduced_idx)\n        if keepdims:\n            assert len(index) == len(size)\n            index = [index[i] for i in kept_idx]\n        assert len(index) == len(kept_idx)\n        new_index = [None] * (len(index) + len(reduction_index))\n        for idx, var in itertools.chain(\n            zip(kept_idx, index), isinstance(x, TensorBox)\n    assert isinstance(size, (list, tuple))\n\n    if memory_format is None:\n        memory_format = torch.contiguous_format\n    if memory_format == torch.preserve_format:\n        raise RuntimeError(f\"unsupported memory format: {memory_format}\")\n\n    if memory_format == torch.channels_last:\n        assert len(size) == 4\n    if memory_format == torch.channels_last_3d:\n        assert len(size) == 5\n\n    old_numel = x.get_numel()\n    dtype = x.get_dtype()\n    device = x.get_device_or_error()\n\n    if isinstance(x.data, ir.BaseView):\n        x.data = x.data.unwrap_view()\n\n    if (\n        torch.are_deterministic_algorithms_enabled()\n        and torch.utils.deterministic.fill_uninitialized_memory  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n    ):\n        if is_float_dtype(dtype):\n            uninitialized_val = float(\"nan\")\n        elif is_integer_dtype(dtype):\n            uninitialized_val = torch.iinfo(dtype).max\n        else:\n            uninitialized_val = True\n    else:\n        # using zero as that is what empty does\n        uninitialized_val = 0.0\n\n    if V.graph.sizevars.statically_known_equals(old_numel, 0):  # type: list(map(TensorBox.create, result))  # type: ignore[call-overload]\n\n\ndef process_subgraph_nodes(graph_module: torch.fx.GraphModule, args: list[Any]):\n    \"\"\"Process nodes from a FX graph by executing them through V.graph.\n\n    This is a common pattern for executing a subgraph's nodes:\n    - Placeholder nodes are mapped to the provided args\n    - Output nodes return their result\n    - Other nodes are executed via V.graph.run_node\n\n    \"\"\"\n    output = None\n\n    for i, node in enumerate(graph_module.graph.nodes):\n        if node.op == \"placeholder\":\n            assert node not in V.graph.env\n            V.graph.env[node] = args[i]\n            continue\n        elif node.op == \"output\":\n            output_args, kwargs = V.graph.fetch_args_kwargs_from_env(node)\n            output = torch.fx.Interpreter.output(V.graph, node, output_args, kwargs)\n        else:\n            assert node not in V.graph.env\n            V.graph.env[node] = V.graph.run_node(node)\n\n    if output is None:\n        raise RuntimeError(\"No output node found in graph\")\n\n    return output\n\n\n# Import the control_deps_op HOP for lowering\nfrom torch._inductor.fx_passes.control_dependencies import control_deps\n\n\n@register_lowering(control_deps, type_promotion_kind=None)\ndef control_deps_op_lowering(additional_deps, subgraph_fn, *args):\n    \"\"\"\n    Lower control_deps_op by ensuring dependencies are realized and tracking them.\n\n    The control_deps_op HOP makes dependencies explicit in the graph. During lowering:\n    1. Realize all additional dependencies to ensure they're computed\n    2. Execute the target operation normally\n    3. Track the dependencies for the scheduler\n    \"\"\"\n    # Realize all additional dependencies\n    dep_names = []\n    for dep in additional_deps:\n        if not isinstance(dep, IRNode):\n            continue\n\n        dep.realize()\n        dep_names.append(dep.get_name())\n\n    original_args = V.graph.current_node.args\n    arg_offset = 2  # first two args (additional_deps, subgraph)\n    assert len(args) + arg_offset == len(original_args)\n\n    operation_len = len(V.graph.operations)\n    assert len(subgraph_fn.graph_module.graph.find_nodes(op=\"placeholder\")) == len(args)\n\n    # Process subgraph nodes using the shared helper\n    output = process_subgraph_nodes(subgraph_fn.graph_module, list(args))\n\n    assert output is not None and additional_deps\n\n    # some operators, like wait_tensor, just return their input,\n    # x1.pow(2).sum(-1, True)\n    x1_pad = torch.ones_like(x1_norm, memory_format=torch.contiguous_format)\n    x2_norm = x2.pow(2).sum(-1, True)\n    x2_pad = torch.ones_like(x2_norm, memory_format=torch.contiguous_format)\n    x1_ = torch.cat([x1.mul(-2), x1_norm, x1_pad], -1)\n    x2_ = torch.cat([x2, x2_pad, x2_norm], -1)\n    result = x1_.matmul(x2_.mT)\n    return   start: Optional[int] = None,\n    end: Optional[int] = None,\n    step: int = 1,\n):\n    from torch.fx.experimental.symbolic_shapes import statically_known_true\n\n    ndim = self.dim()\n    if ndim == 0:\n        raise RuntimeError(\"slice() cannot be applied to a 0-dim tensor.\")\n    dim = utils.canonicalize_dim(self.dim(), dim)\n    sizes = list(self.size())\n    strides = sys.maxsize  # 2^63 - 1\n\n    if start_val < 0:\n        start_val += sizes[dim]\n\n    if end_val < 0:\n        end_val += sizes[dim]\n\n    if start_val < 0:\n        start_val = 0\n    elif start_val > sizes[dim]:\n        start_val = sizes[dim]\n\n    if statically_known_true(end_val == sys.maxsize):\n        end_val = sizes[dim]\n    elif end_val < start_val:\n        end_val = step - 1) // step\n    strides[dim] *= step\n\n    if self.is_quantized:\n        raise NotImplementedError(\n            \"Slice decomposition for quantized tensors aren't implemented\"\n        )\n    else:\n        return self.as_strided(sizes, strides, storage_offset)\n\n\ndef _normalize_start_end(\n    x: Tensor, dim: int, start: Optional[int], end: Optional[int]\n) -> tuple[int, int]:\n    \"\"\"\n    Normalize start and end such that both are in the range\n    [0, x.get_size()[dim]] and start <= end.\n    \"\"\"\n    dim_size = x.shape[dim]\n\n    def clamp_wrap(val, lower, upper, default) -> int:\n        if val is None:\n            return default\n        if val < 0:\n            val = val + dim_size\n        return min(max(val, lower), upper)\n\n    start = clamp_wrap(start, 0, dim_size, 0)\n    end = clamp_wrap(end, start, dim_size, dim_size)\n    return start, end\n\n\n# This is not in torch._refs because aten.index used by\n# aten._unsafe_masked_index does not have a decomposition.\n@register_decomposition(aten.slice_scatter)\n@out_wrapper()\ndef slice_scatter(\n    input: Tensor,\n    src: Tensor,\n    dim: int = 0,\n    start: Optional[int] = None,\n    end: Optional[int] = None,\n    step: int = 1,\n):\n    dim = utils.canonicalize_dim(input.ndim, dim)\n    dim_size = input.shape[dim]\n    start, end = _normalize_start_end(input, dim, start, end)\n\n    src_size = list(input.shape)\n    src_size[dim] = (end - start + (step - 1)) // step\n    src = src.expand(src_size)\n\n    if start == 0 and end == dim_size and step == 1:\n        return src.clone()\n\n    indices: list[Optional[Tensor]] = [None] * input.dim()\n    idx = torch.arange(dim_size, device=input.device)\n    indices[dim] = (idx - start) // step\n\n    mask = torch.ones(dim_size, device=input.device, dtype=torch.bool)\n    if start != 0:\n        mask = torch.logical_and(mask, idx >= start)\n\n    if end != dim_size:\n        mask = torch.logical_and(mask, idx < end)\n\n    if step != 1:\n        mask = torch.logical_and(mask, (idx - start) % step == 0)\n\n    mask_shape = [1] * input.dim()\n    mask_shape[dim] = -1\n    mask = mask.view(mask_shape)\n function to implement im2col and col2im\"\"\"\n    blocks_d = input_d + padding_d * 2 - dilation_d * (kernel_d - 1)\n\n    arange_kw = partial(torch.arange, dtype=torch.int64, device=device)\n\n    # \"stride\")\n    check_positive(output_size, \"output_size\")\n\n    shape = input.shape\n    ndim = len(shape)\n    torch._check(\n        ndim in (2, 3) and all(d != 0 for d in shape[-2:]),\n        lambda: \"Expected 2D or 3D (batch mode) tensor for input with possible 0 batch size \"\n        f\"and non-zero dimensions, but got: {tuple(shape)}\",\n    )\n    prod_kernel_size = kernel_size[0] * kernel_size[1]\n    torch._check(\n        shape[-2] % prod_kernel_size == 0,\n        lambda: \"Expected size of input's first non-batch dimension to be divisible by the \"\n        f\"product of kernel_size, but got input.shape[-2] = {shape[-2]} and \"\n        f\"kernel_size={kernel_size}\",\n    )\n    col = [\n        1 + (out + 2 * pad - dil * (ker - 1) - 1) // st\n        for out, pad, dil, ker, st in zip(\n            output_size, padding, dilation, kernel_size, stride\n        )\n    ]\n    L = col[0] * col[1]\n    torch._check(\n        shape[-1] == L,\n        lambda: f\"Given output_size={output_size}, kernel_size={kernel_size}, \"\n        f\"dilation={dilation}, padding={padding}, stride={stride}, \"\n        f\"expected input.size(-1) to be {L} but got {shape[-1]}.\",\n    )\n    torch._check(\n        L > 0,\n        lambda: f\"Given output_size={output_size}, kernel_size={kernel_size}, \"\n        f\"dilation={dilation}, padding={padding}, stride={stride}, \"\n        f\"expected input.size(-1) to be {L} but got {shape[-1]}.\",\n    )\n    batched_input = ndim == 3\n    if not batched_input:\n        input = input.unsqueeze(0)\n\n    shape = input.shape\n\n    out_h, out_w = output_size\n    stride_h, stride_w = stride\n    padding_h, padding_w = padding\n    dilation_h, dilation_w = dilation\n    kernel_h, kernel_w = kernel_size\n\n    # col2im is defined as the backwards of im2col, so we differentiate its decomposition by hand\n    input = input.reshape([shape[0], shape[1] // prod_kernel_size] + kernel_size + col)\n    input = input.permute(0, 1, 2, 4, 3, 5)\n\n    indices_row = _im2col_col2im_indices_along_dim(\n        out_h, kernel_h, dilation_h, padding_h, stride_h, input.device\n    )\n    indices_row = _unsqueeze_to_dim(indices_row, 4)\n    indices_col = _im2col_col2im_indices_along_dim(\n        out_w, kernel_w, dilation_w, padding_w, stride_w, input.device\n    )\n\n    output_padded_size = [o + 2 * p for o, p in zip(output_size, padding)]\n    output = input.new_zeros(\n        [shape[0], shape[1] // prod(kernel_size)] + output_padded_size\n    )\n    idx = (None, None, indices_row, indices_col)\n    output = aten._unsafe_index_put(output, idx, input, accumulate=True)\n    output = F.pad(output, (-padding_w, -padding_w, -padding_h, -padding_h))\n\n    if not batched_input:\n        output = output.squeeze(0)\n    return output\n\n\n@register_decomposition(aten.native_dropout_backward)\n@out_wrapper()\ndef native_dropout_backward(grad_output: Tensor, mask: Tensor, scale: float):\n    # According to the CUDA kernel implementation we should have this test;\n    # but it seems to fail tests!\n    # torch._check(mask.dtype == torch.bool, lambda: f\"Mask should be Bool Scalar Type {mask.dtype}\")\n\n    # Mimicking CUDA kernel's behavior for output stride: output follow input's memory format\n    # This different from TensorIterator's behavior\n    r = (grad_output * unfold_backward(\n    grad: Tensor, input_size: list[int], dimension: int, size: int, step: int\n) -> Tensor:\n    if len(input_size) == 0:\n        return torch.squeeze_copy(grad, 0)\n    dim = lo\n        return torch.where(\n            torch.logical_and(self >= lo, self <= hi),\n            grad_output / (self * (1.0 - self)),\n            0.0,\n        )\n    else:\n        return torch.where(\n            torch.logical_and(self >= 0.0, self <= 1.0),\n            grad_output / (self * (1.0 - Ensure that decomp also returns\n    # a contiguous tensor.\n    x = x.contiguous()\n    if half_to_float:\n        assert x.dtype == torch.half\n    computation_dtype, result_dtype = utils.elementwise_dtypes(\n        x, type_promotion_kind=utils.ELEMENTWISE_TYPE_PROMOTION_KIND.DEFAULT\n    )\n    x = x.to(computation_dtype)\n    if guard_or_false(x.numel() == 0):\n        unnormalized = torch.exp(x)\n    else:\n        x_max = torch.amax(x, dim, keepdim=True)\n        unnormalized = torch.exp(x - x_max)\n    result = unnormalized / torch.sum(unnormalized, dim, keepdim=True)\n    if not half_to_float:\n        result = result.to(result_dtype)\n    return result\n\n\n@register_decomposition(aten._log_softmax)\n@out_wrapper(exact_dtype=True)\ndef _log_softmax(x: Tensor, dim: int, half_to_float: bool):\n    from torch.fx.experimental.symbolic_shapes import guard_or_false\n\n    # eager log_softmax returns a contiguous tensor. bfloat16\n@register_decomposition(aten.addmm)\n@out_wrapper(exact_dtype=True)\n@pw_cast_for_opmath\ndef addmm(self: Tensor, mat1: Tensor, mat2: Tensor, beta: int = 1, alpha: int = 1):\n    if not self.is_floating_point() and not self.is_complex():\n        beta = int(beta)\n        alpha = int(alpha)\n    out = alpha * torch.mm(mat1, mat2)\n    if beta == 0:\n        return out\n\n    # The output of aten.addmm is contiguous, we need to match this behavior in the decomposition.\n    # The original implementation 'beta * self + out' would return a strided tensor if `self` is strided.\n    # We thus use `out`, the output of torch.mm, which is always contiguous, as the first argument for addition.\n    # This is relying on TensorIterator's behavior that it takes higher precedence on the stride of first input.\n    # Alternative, we can write `(beta * self + out).contiguous()`, but it introduces another copy in some cases.\n    # This implementation is not ideal, and we should revisit this when we have a better solution.\n    return out + beta * self\n\n\n@register_decomposition(aten._addmm_activation)\n@out_wrapper()\n@pw_cast_for_opmath\ndef _addmm_activation(\n    self: aten.relu(out)\n\n\n@register_decomposition(aten.addmv)\n@out_wrapper(exact_dtype=True)\n@pw_cast_for_opmath\ndef addmv(self: Tensor, mat1: Tensor, vec: Tensor, beta: int = 1, alpha: int = 1):\n    if native_group_norm_backward(\n    grad_output: Tensor,\n    input: Tensor,\n    mean: Tensor,\n    rstd: Tensor,\n    gamma: Optional[Tensor],\n    N: int,\n    C: int,\n    HxW: int,\n    group: int,\n    output_mask: list[bool],\n) -> tuple[Optional[Tensor], Optional[Tensor], Optional[Tensor]]:\n    utils.check_same_device(\n        grad_output, input, mean, rstd, got {gamma.numel() if gamma is not None else -1}\",\n    )\n\n    cpg = C // group\n    torch._check(\n        C == cpg * group,\n        lambda: f\"Expect number of channels {C} to be evenly-divisible by number of groups {group}\",\n    )\n\n    # Compute Internal gradients\n    ds = torch.mul(grad_output, input).view(N, C, HxW).sum(dim=[2])\n    db = grad_output.view(N, C, HxW).sum(dim=[2])\n\n    d_input: Optional[Tensor] = None\n    d_gamma: Optional[Tensor] = None\n    d_bias: Optional[Tensor] = None\n    if output_mask[0]:\n        s = 1.0 / (HxW * cpg)\n        if gamma is not None:\n            ds_val = torch.mul(ds, gamma.unsqueeze(0)).reshape(N, group, cpg).sum(2)\n            db_val = torch.mul(db, gamma.unsqueeze(0)).reshape(N, group, cpg).sum(2)\n            c1 = torch.mul(\n                rstd.unsqueeze(-1),\n                gamma.reshape(1, group, cpg),\n            )\n        else:\n            ds_val = ds.reshape(N, group, cpg).sum(2)\n            db_val = db.reshape(N, group, cpg).sum(2)\n            c1 = torch.mul(\n                rstd.unsqueeze(-1),\n                torch.ones((1, group, cpg), device=rstd.device),\n            )\n        c2 = (db_val * mean - ds_val) * rstd * rstd * rstd * s\n        c3 = -c2 * mean - db_val * rstd * s\n\n        c1 = c1.unsqueeze(-1)\n        c2 = _unsqueeze_to_dim(c2, 4)\n        c3 =     )\n        d_input = d_input.reshape(input.shape).to(input.dtype)\n    if output_mask[1]:\n        d_gamma = (\n            (\n                (ds.view(N, group, cpg) - db.view(N, group, cpg) * = []\n    for i in range(input_ndim):\n        if i >= axis:\n            inner_dim_indices.append(i)\n        else:\n            outer_dim_indices.append(i)\n\n    N = prod(inner_dims)  # type:           input.new_zeros(input_shape[axis:]) if output_mask[2] else None,\n        )\n    mean = _unsqueeze_to_dim(mean, input_cast.dim())  # type: ignore[union-attr]\n    rstd = c2 = torch.sum(c1, inner_dim_indices, True)\n    c3 = torch.mul(x_hat, c2)\n\n    inner = a - b - c3\n    d_input: Optional[Tensor] = None\n    d_weight: Optional[Tensor] = None\n    d_bias: Tensor,\n    normalized_shape: list[int],\n    weight: Optional[Tensor],\n    eps: Optional[float],\n) -> tuple[Tensor, Tensor]:\n    dims_to_reduce: list[int] = []\n    for i in (torch.float32, torch.complex64):\n            eps_val = torch.finfo(torch.float32).eps\n        else:\n            eps_val = torch.finfo(torch.float64).eps\n    else:\n        eps_val = eps\n\n    rqrst_input = torch.rsqrt(\n        # NB: don't inplace here, will violate functional IR invariant\n        # NB: carefully use the Scalar overload of add to ensure compatibility with the C++ decomp\n        torch.ops.aten.add.Scalar(\n            torch.pow(upcasted_input, 2).mean(dim=dims_to_reduce, keepdim=True), eps_val\n        )\n    )\n\n    upcasted_result = torch.channels_last_3d,\n    )\n\n    if not is_nested and not is_channels_last:\n        upcasted_result = upcasted_result.contiguous()\n        rqrst_input = rqrst_input.contiguous()\n\n    # Cast _fused_rms_norm_backward(\n    grad_out: Tensor,\n    input: Tensor,\n    normalized_shape: list[int],\n    rstd: Tensor,\n    weight: Optional[Tensor],\n    output_mask: list[bool],\n) -> tuple[Optional[Tensor], Optional[Tensor]]:\n    input_shape = input.shape\n    input_ndim = input.dim()\n    computation_dtype = utils.get_computation_dtype(input.dtype)\n\n    grad_out_cast = grad_out.to(\n        computation_dtype, memory_format=torch.contiguous_format\n    )\n    input_cast = input.to(computation_dtype, memory_format=torch.contiguous_format)\n    weight_cast = (\n        weight.to(computation_dtype, memory_format=torch.contiguous_format)\n        if weight is not None\n        else None\n    )\n    assert grad_out_cast is not None\n\n    axis = input_ndim -      input.new_zeros(input_shape) if output_mask[0] else None,\n            input.new_zeros(input_shape[axis:]) if output_mask[1] else None,\n        )\n\n    rstd = _unsqueeze_to_dim(rstd, Optional[Tensor],\n    bias: Optional[Tensor],\n    running_mean: Optional[Tensor],\n    running_var: Optional[Tensor],\n    training: bool,\n    momentum: float,\n    eps: float,\n    functional: bool,\n) -> tuple[Tensor, Tensor, Tensor, Optional[Tensor], Optional[Tensor]]:\n    reduction_dims = [0] + list(range(2, input.dim()))\n    computation_dtype = utils.get_computation_dtype(input.dtype)\n    new_running_mean = running_mean\n    new_running_var = running_var\n    if training:\n        computation_dtype = utils.get_computation_dtype(input.dtype)\n        input_acc = input.to(dtype=computation_dtype)\n        biased_var, mean = torch.var_mean(\n            input_acc, dim=reduction_dims, correction=0, keepdim=True\n        )\n        rstd = torch.rsqrt(biased_var + eps)\n\n        output = (input - mean) * rstd\n\n        save_mean = torch.squeeze(mean, reduction_dims)\n        save_rstd = torch.squeeze(rstd, reduction_dims)\n        if running_mean is not None:\n            new_running_mean = momentum * save_mean + (1 - momentum) * running_mean\n            if not functional:\n                running_mean.copy_(new_running_mean)\n        if running_var is not None:\n            n = input.numel() / input.shape[1]\n            # This doesn't strictly match eager's numerics, which accumulates var sum and then directly applies the correction\n            # But... that would require re-implementing var here, for negligible numerics gain on a tensor whose\n            # numerics probably don't matter.\n            squeezed_var = torch.squeeze(biased_var, reduction_dims)\n            unbiased_var = squeezed_var * (n / (n - 1))\n            new_running_var = momentum * unbiased_var + (1 - momentum) * running_var\n            if not functional:\n                running_var.copy_(new_running_var)\n    else:\n        assert running_mean is not None and running_var is not None\n        running_mean = running_mean.to(dtype=computation_dtype, copy=True)\n        new_running_mean = running_mean\n        running_var = running_var.to(dtype=computation_dtype, copy=True)\n        new_running_var = running_var\n        mean = running_mean\n        invstd = 1 / (torch.sqrt(running_var + eps))\n        # Very annoying inconsistency where CPU and CUDA give different shapes\n        if input.device.type != \"cpu\":\n            save_mean = running_mean\n            save_rstd = invstd\n        else:\n            save_mean = input.new_zeros((0,))\n            save_rstd = input.new_zeros((0,))\n        mean = _unsqueeze_to_dim(mean, input.dim() - 1)\n        invstd = _unsqueeze_to_dim(invstd, input.dim() - 1)\n        output = (input - mean) * invstd\n\n    if weight is not None:\n        weight = weight.flatten()\n        weight = _unsqueeze_to_dim(weight, input.dim() - 1)\n        output = output * weight\n\n    if bias is not None:\n        bias = bias.flatten()\n        bias = _unsqueeze_to_dim(bias, input.dim() - 1)\n        output = output + bias\n\n    if input.device.type == \"cpu\":\n        save_mean = save_mean.to(dtype=input.dtype)\n        save_rstd = save_rstd.to(dtype=input.dtype)\n    return (\n        output.to(dtype=input.dtype),\n        save_mean,\n        save_rstd,\n        new_running_mean,\n        new_running_var,\n    )\n\n\n@register_decomposition(aten.native_batch_norm)\n@out_wrapper(\"out\", \"save_mean\", \"save_invstd\")\ndef native_batch_norm(\n    input: Tensor,\n    weight: Optional[Tensor],\n    bias: = x.unsqueeze(axis)\n    return x\n\n\n@register_decomposition(aten.batch_norm_backward.default)\ndef batch_norm_backward(\n    grad_out: Tensor,\n    input: Tensor,\n    weight: Optional[Tensor],\n )\n\n\n@register_decomposition(aten.native_batch_norm_backward.default)\ndef native_batch_norm_backward(\n    grad_out: Tensor,\n    input: Tensor,\n    weight: Optional[Tensor],\n    running_mean: Optional[Tensor],\n    running_var: Optional[Tensor],\n    save_mean: Optional[Tensor],\n    save_invstd: Optional[Tensor],\n    train: bool,\n    eps: float,\n    output_mask: list[bool],\n) -> tuple[Tensor, Optional[Tensor], Optional[Tensor]]:\n    input_dtype = input.dtype\n    if weight is not None:\n        weight_dtype = weight.dtype\n    else:\n        weight_dtype = input_dtype\n    computation_dtype = utils.get_computation_dtype(input.dtype)\n    (\n        grad_out_cast,\n        input_cast,\n        weight_cast,\n        running_mean_cast,\n        running_var_cast,\n        save_mean_cast,\n        save_invstd_cast,\n    ) = (\n        x.to(computation_dtype) if x is not None else x\n        for x in (\n            grad_out,\n            input,\n            weight,\n            running_mean,\n            running_var,\n            save_mean,\n            save_invstd,\n        )\n    )\n    input_shape = input.shape\n    input_rank = input.dim()\n    assert input_rank >= 2, \"rank of the input must be at least 2\"\n\n    axis = 1\n    num_features = prod(list(input_shape)) / input_shape[axis]\n    mean = save_mean_cast\n    invstd = save_invstd_cast\n    if train:\n        assert mean is not None and invstd is not None\n\n    else:\n        assert running_mean_cast is not None and running_var_cast is not None\n        mean = running_mean_cast\n        invstd = torch.rsqrt(running_var_cast + eps)\n\n    broadcast_mask: list[int] = [1] * input_rank\n    broadcast_mask[axis] = input_shape[axis]\n\n    reduction_axes: list[int] = []\n    for i in range(input_rank):\n        if i != axis:\n            reduction_axes.append(i)\n\n    mean = _broadcast_batch_norm_backward(mean, broadcast_mask)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n    norm = 1.0 / num_features\n    grad_output_sum = torch.sum(grad_out_cast, reduction_axes)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n    dot_p = torch.sum(grad_out_cast * (input_cast - mean), reduction_axes)  # type: ignore[operator]\n\n    grad_mean = _broadcast_batch_norm_backward(grad_output_sum * norm, broadcast_mask)\n    proj_scale = _broadcast_batch_norm_backward(\n        torch.mul(dot_p * norm, invstd * invstd),  # type: ignore[operator]\n        broadcast_mask,\n    )\n\n    if weight_cast is None:\n        grad_scale = _broadcast_batch_norm_backward(invstd, broadcast_mask) * 1.0  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n    else:\n        grad_scale = _broadcast_batch_norm_backward(\n            invstd * weight_cast, broadcast_mask\n        )\n\n    if train:\n        proj = (input_cast - mean) * proj_scale  # type: ignore[operator]\n        grad_input = ((grad_out_cast - proj) - grad_mean) * grad_scale\n    else:\n        grad_input = grad_out_cast * grad_scale\n\n    if output_mask[1]:\n        grad_weight = dot_p * invstd\n    else:\n        grad_weight = None  # \"None\" doesn't work with vjp, should use zeros for vjp\n\n    if output_mask[2]:\n        grad_bias = grad_output_sum\n    else:\n        grad_bias = None  # \"None\" doesn't work with vjp, should use zeros for vjp\n\n    return (\n        grad_input.to(input_dtype),\n        _maybe_cast(grad_weight, weight_dtype),\n        _maybe_cast(grad_bias, weight_dtype),\n    )\n\n\n# out_wrapper currently does not allow optional outputs\n@register_decomposition(aten.native_batch_norm_backward.out)\ndef
